Considering the fact that Pyn-Jeju5 has been taxonomically classified as Pyn based on morphological characters, highly precise tools such as molecular markers should be utilized to correctly identify Pyn for evaluation and conservation of this taxon in nature.</p><p>For reproduction of <i>Prunus</i> species, successful pollination, fertilization, and seed formation are indispensable since parthenocarpic fruits have not developed in <i>Prunus</i> species. Our comparative genome analysis indicated that diversification of the <i>Prunus</i> genomes arose during the Paleocene (up to 66 Mya), followed by the successive split of <i>Prunus</i> species during the Eocene (36–44 Mya). This result is supported by the discovery of fossilized endocarps of <i>P. wutuensis</i> in eastern Asia dating to the Eocene [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="Li Y, Smith T, Liu C-J, Awasthi N, Yang J, Wang Y-F, et al. Endocarps of Prunus (Rosaceae: Prunoideae) from the early Eocene of Wutu, Shandong Province, China. Taxon. 2011;60:555–64." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4621">32</a>]. Expansion of a specific category of genes related to auxin response and early flowering may have been involved in the diversification of flowering <i>Prunus</i> species. In addition, characterization of S-locus haplotypes, the determinant of <i>Prunus</i> GSI, in Pyn and its related species has yielded novel insights into the inter-specific hybridization of flowering <i>Prunus</i> in sympatric regions. All the flowering <i>Prunus</i> accessions investigated in this study had unique pairs of heterozygous S haplotypes that suggested out-breeding. Nevertheless, two Pyn accessions retained a combination of parental S haplotypes, each of which was shared with one parental lineage, and several S haplotypes were also shared between accessions or even different taxa (Psa and Pjq). Considering the fact that these taxa are sympatrically distributed in a 3 km range on Jeju Island, and that their blooming time (late-March to mid-April) and flowering periods (approximately two weeks) overlap, we anticipate that cross pollination between closely related taxa resulted in a hybridization network of flowering <i>Prunus</i> in this natural habitat. These findings are consistent with our previous hypothesis that inter-specific hybridization and additional introgression by backcross between closely related flowering <i>Prunus</i> species on Jeju Island may produce a hybrid swarm [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 24" title="Cho A, Baek S, Kim G-B, Shin C-H, Kim C-S, Choi K, et al. Genomic clues to the parental origin of the wild flowering cherry Prunus yedoensis var. nudiflora (Rosaceae). Plant Biotechnol Rep. 2017;11:449–59." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4643">24</a>]. Therefore, we anticipate that reproductive barriers between closely related flowering <i>Prunus</i> genomes are likely to be unestablished, presumably due to strong GSI, resulting in reduced restriction of inter-specific hybridization.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec11" data-title="Conclusions"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec11-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec11">Conclusions</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec11-content"><p>Hybridization has greatly increased plant diversity by generating new genetic combinations and genomes. However, the highly heterozygous genomic nature of hybrid species complicates genome studies due to the presence of highly similar sequences, a significant challenge in plant genomics. In this study, we successfully sequenced and assembled the draft genome of <i>P. yedoensis</i> var. <i>nudiflora</i>, a wild hybrid taxon of flowering <i>Prunus</i>, using long-read sequencing and a sequence phasing strategy. The results suggest that inter-specific hybridization due to the strong gametophytic self-incompatibility of flowering <i>Prunus</i> species may have contributed to the establishment of a natural hybrid taxon. The genome assembly of this taxon, along with the whole-genome resequencing data of related <i>Prunus</i> taxa, will provide valuable genomic resources for research, conservation, and breeding studies of <i>Prunus</i> species, benefiting both basic and applied plant biologists.</p></div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Sec12" data-title="Methods"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec12-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec12">Methods</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec12-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec13">Plant material and genome sequencing</h3><p>The No. 2 accession at the natural habitat of <i>P. yedoensis</i> var. <i>nudiflora</i> in Bongae-dong, Jeju Island (the Korea National Monument No. 159, Pyn<i>-</i>Jeju2; Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#Fig1">1a</a>) was chosen for genome sequencing. It was estimated to be 200 years old. Genomic DNA (gDNA) was extracted from young leaves collected in April 2015 using a DNeasy Plant Maxi Kit (Qiagen, Valencia, CA, USA) and then used for short-read sequencing. Separately, high molecular weight DNA was isolated according to the nuclei isolation method for single-molecule sequencing [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 33" title="Zhang M, Zhang Y, Scheuring C, Wu C, Dong J, Zhang H. Preparation of megabase-sized DNA from a variety of organisms using the nuclei method for advanced genomics research. Nat Protoc. 2012;7:467–78." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR33" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4700">33</a>]. In total, 325.3 Gb of sequence data was obtained using Illumina and PacBio platforms (Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#MOESM2">2</a>: Table S1) according to the manufacturer’s protocols. For short-read sequencing, 205.5 Gb of Illumina sequences was generated using NextSeq and MiSeq (Illumina, San Diego, CA, USA) sequencing of 250-base pair (bp) (NextSeq) and 500-bp (MiSeq) insert libraries for PE sequencing and 3-, 5-, 10-, 15-, and 20-kb insert libraries for MP sequencing. In addition, one Fosmid library consisting of 55,200 clones with an average insert size of 40 kb (8.6×) was constructed using the NxSeq 40 kb Mate pair cloning kit (Lucigen, Middleton, WI, USA). Fosmid-end sequences were generated using HiSeq X Ten (Illumina, San Diego, CA, USA). Illumina reads from each library were collected at a minimum quality score (Q20) and then filtered for adaptor contamination and low-quality regions using Trimmomatic v0.32 software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 34" title="Bolger A, Lohse M, Usadel B. Trimmomatic: a flexible trimmer for Illumina sequence data. Bioinformatics. 2014;30:2114–020." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4707">34</a>]. Polymerase chain reaction (PCR) duplicates were removed by FastUniq v1.1 software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 35" title="Xu H, Luo X, Qian J, Pang X, Song J, Qian G, et al. FastUniq: a fast de novo duplicates removal tool for paired short reads. PLoS One. 2012;7:e52249." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4710">35</a>] with a default parameter. Adaptor sequences and PCR duplicates of MP reads were filtered using NextClip software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 36" title="Leggett R, Clavijo B, Clissold L, Clark M, Caccamo M. NextClip: an analysis and read preparation tool for Nextera long mate pair libraries. Bioinformatics. 2014;30:566–8." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4713">36</a>]. For single-molecule sequencing, 18.8 Gb of PacBio sequences was generated from a 20-kb library using a PacBio RSII sequencer (Pacific Biosciences, Menlo Park, CA, USA) and sequence errors were corrected using the PBcR pipeline from Celera Assembler 8.3.1 software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 37" title="Berlin K, Koren S, Chin C, Drake J, Landolin J, Phillippy A. Assembling large genomes with single-molecule sequencing and locality-sensitive hashing. Nat Biotechnol. 2015;33:623–30." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4716">37</a>] with default parameters. All of the sequence data generated in this study are summarized in Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#MOESM2">2</a>: Table S1.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec14">Genome size estimation and de novo assembly</h3><p>The genome size of Pyn was estimated both by flow cytometry and K-mer analysis. For flow cytometry analysis, genome size was measured according to previous reports [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 38" title="Hwang Y-J, Yu H-J, Mun J-H, Ryu K, Park B-S, Lim K-B. Centromere repeat DNA originated from Brassica rapa is detected in the centromere region of Raphanus sativus chromosomes. Kor J Hort Sci Technol. 2012;30:751–6." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4730">38</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 39" title="Dolezel J, Bartos J, Voglmayr H, Greilhuber J. Nuclear DNA content and genome size of trout and human. Cytometry A. 2003;51:127–8." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4733">39</a>] using a CyFlow Space system (Partec BmbH, Münster, Germany) and diploid <i>Raphanus sativus</i> cv. WK10039 (1C = 0.6 pg) as a reference. For K-mer analysis, the occurrences of K-mer with a peak depth were counted using Illumina PE reads, and genome size was calculated by dividing the total read length by coverage of K-mer peak using JELLYFISH 2.1.3 software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 40" title="Marçais G, Kingsford C. A fast, lock-free approach for efficient parallel counting of occurrences of k-mers. Bioinformatics. 2011;27:764–70." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4739">40</a>] with K-mer 17. To assemble the sequence reads into a draft genome, a hierarchical hybrid assembly strategy was used (Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#MOESM1">1</a>: Figure S2). First, PacBio reads were assembled into the initial scaffolds using the FALCON assembler v0.3.0 with parameters of length cutoff 12 kb, max difference 100, max coverage 150, and minimum coverage 2. The initial scaffolds were filtered with chloroplast and mitochondrial sequences using NUCmer in the MUMmer 3 package [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="Kurtz S, Phillippy A, Delcher A, Smoot M, Shumway M, Antonescu C, et al. Versatile and open software for comparing large genomes. Genome Biol. 2004;5:R12." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4746">41</a>]. Next, Illumina reads were assembled with the chloroplast and mitochondria-filtered scaffolds to extend the scaffolds using SOAPdenovo2.04 software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 42" title="Luo R, Liu B, Xie Y, Li Z, Huang W, Yuan J, et al. SOAPdenovo2: an empirically improved memory-efficient short-read de novo assembler. Gigascience. 2012;1:18." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4749">42</a>]. The resulting scaffolds were aligned with PacBio reads that had not been assembled into the initial scaffolds for additional assembly and gap filling using PBJelly 15.2.20 software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 43" title="English A, Richards S, Han Y, Wang M, Vee V, Qu J, et al. Mind the gap: upgrading genomes with Pacific biosciences RS long-read sequencing technology. PLoS One. 2012;7:e47768." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4752">43</a>] with minMatch 8, minimum identity 70, maxScore 500, noSplitSubreads, and support stage–capturedOnly parameters. Finally, draft assembly was improved by Pilon software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Walker B, Abeel T, Shea T, Priest M, Abouelliel A, Sakthikumar S, et al. Pilon: an integrated tool for comprehensive microbial variant detection and genome assembly improvement. PLoS One. 2014;9:e112963." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4755">44</a>] for additional gap filling and sequence error correction with fix bases, gaps, and diploid parameters.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec15">Genome annotation</h3><p>For gene prediction, a combination of ab initio and evidence-based gene predictions was used. The genome assembly was premasked first for class I and class II transposons using RepeatMasker 4.0.5 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 45" title="RepeatMasker 4.0.5. &#xA;                    http://www.repeatmasker.org&#xA;                    &#xA;                  . Accessed 24 June 2016." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4766">45</a>], RepeatModeler 1.0.8 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 46" title="RepeatModeler. &#xA;                    http://www.repeatmasker.org&#xA;                    &#xA;                  . Accessed 24 June 2016." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4769">46</a>], and LTR_FINDER v1.05 software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 47" title="Xu Z, Wang H. LTR_FINDER: an efficient tool for the prediction of full-length LTR retrotransposons. Nucleic Acids Res. 2007;35:W265–8." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4772">47</a>], then protein-coding genes were predicted ab initio using BRAKER1 v1.8 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Hoff K, Lange S, Lomsadze A, Borodovsky M, Stanke M. BRAKER1: unsupervised RNA-Seq-based genome annotation with GeneMark-ET and AUGUSTUS. Bioinformatics. 2016;32:767–9." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4775">48</a>], GlimmerHMM v3.0.2 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Majoros W, Pertea M, Salzberg S. TigrScan and GlimmerHMM: two open source ab initio eukaryotic gene-finders. Bioinformatics. 2004;20:2878–9." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4778">49</a>], and SNAP [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Korf I. Gene finding in novel genomes. BMC Bioinformatics. 2004;5:59." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4782">50</a>] programs with parameters trained using the <i>A. thaliana</i> matrix. Genes with &lt; 300 bp of coding sequence or an incomplete coding region were filtered out. Predicted proteins with a top match to transposon-encoded proteins [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Nussbaumer T, Martis M, Roessner S, Pfeifer M, Bader K, Sharma S, et al. MIPS PlantsDB: a database framework for comparative plant genome research. Nucleic Acids Res. 2013;41:D1144–51." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4788">51</a>] and putative gene splits predicted on the unfinished gaps were also excluded from the annotation and gene counts. For evidence-based gene prediction, seven tissues, including floral bud, foliar bud, leaf, petal, stamen, pistil, and berry, were used to generate approximately 223.7 million filtered Illumina PE mRNA-seq reads (Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#MOESM3">3</a>: Table S2). Total RNA was isolated from each tissue using the cetyl trimethylammonium bromide (CTAB) method [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Chang S, Puryear J, Cairney J. A simple and efficient method for isolating RNA from pine trees. Plant Mol Biol Rep. 1993;11:113–6." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4794">52</a>], which was then used for mRNA purification, construction of a library with a 500-bp insert size, and sequencing according to the manufacturer’s instructions. Quality filtering of mRNA-seq reads was performed according to our previous study [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Jeong Y-M, Kim N, Ahn B, Oh M, Chung W, Chung H, et al. Elucidating the triplicated ancestral genome structure of radish based on chromosome-level comparison with the Brassica genomes. Theor Appl Genet. 2016;129:1357–72." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4797">53</a>]. The resulting transcript sequence data were aligned to the genome assembly and evidence-based gene sets were predicted using the PASA package [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Haas B, Salzberg S, Zhu W, Pertea M, Allen J, Orvis J, et al. Automated eukaryotic gene structure annotation using EVidenceModeler and the program to assemble spliced alignments. Genome Biol. 2008;9:R7." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4801">54</a>]. We also aligned the gene models of Chinese plum (Pm) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Zhang Q, Chen W, Sun L, Zhao F, Huang B, Yang W, et al. The genome of Prunus mume. Nat Commun. 2012;3:1318. &#xA;                    https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/bioproject/171605&#xA;                    &#xA;                  . Accessed 10 Sept 2016" href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4804">9</a>], peach (Pp) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="The International Peach Genome Initiative. The high-quality draft genome of peach (Prunus persica) identifies unique patterns of genetic diversity, domestication and genome evolution. Nat Genet. 2013;45:487–94." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4807">10</a>], strawberry (Fv) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Shulaev V, Sargent D, Crowhurst R, Mockler T, Folkerts O, Delcher A, et al. The genome of woodland strawberry (Fragaria vesca). Nat Genet. 2011;43:109–16." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4810">13</a>], apple (Mxd) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 7" title="Velasco R, Zharkikh A, Affourtit J, Dhingra A, Cestaro A, Kalyanaraman A, et al. The genome of the domesticated apple (Malus × domestica Borkh.). Nat Genet. 2010;42:833–9." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR7" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4813">7</a>], and <i>A. thaliana</i> (TAIR10) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="The Arabidopsis Genome Initiative. Analysis of the genome sequence of the flowering plant Arabidopsis thaliana. Nature. 2000; 408:796–815." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4820">55</a>] to the genome assembly using Exonerate 2.2.0 software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Slater G, Birney E. Automated generation of heuristics for biological sequence comparison. BMC Bioinformatics. 2005;6:31." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4823">56</a>]. EVidenceModeler software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Haas B, Salzberg S, Zhu W, Pertea M, Allen J, Orvis J, et al. Automated eukaryotic gene structure annotation using EVidenceModeler and the program to assemble spliced alignments. Genome Biol. 2008;9:R7." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4826">54</a>] was used to combine ab initio gene models, transcript alignments, and coding sequence alignments into consensus gene model sets. RNA genes were identified using Infernal [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Nawrocki E, Eddy S. Infernal 1.1: 100-fold faster RNA homology searches. Bioinformatics. 2013;29:2933–5." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4829">57</a>] for tRNAs, BLASTN search for rRNAs, and sequence comparison using miRBase [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Griffiths-Jones S, Saini H, van Dongen S, Enright AJ. miRBase: tools for microRNA genomics. Nucleic Acid Res. 2008;36:D154–8." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4832">58</a>] for miRNAs. The predicted protein-coding genes were annotated based on SwissProt and TrEMBL databases from UniProt [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="UniProt. &#xA;                    http://www.ebi.ac.uk/uniprot&#xA;                    &#xA;                  . Accessed 16 Dec 2016." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4835">59</a>], RefSeq Plant, and nucleotide databases of the National Center for Biotechnology Information (NCBI) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="The National Center for Biotechnology Information. &#xA;                    www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov&#xA;                    &#xA;                  ." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4839">60</a>] using BLASTP with an E value cutoff of 1E<sup>−10</sup> and query coverage of 70%. The InterPro database [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="InterPro. &#xA;                    http://www.ebi.ac.uk/interpro&#xA;                    &#xA;                  . Accessed 16 Dec 2016." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4844">61</a>] was also used to annotate motifs and domains and the gene ontology information for each gene model was extracted from InterPro.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec16">Transcriptome and comparative genome analysis</h3><p>Expression analysis of gene models in five tissues (leaf, petal, stamen, pistil, and berry) was performed using the mRNA-seq reads. PE reads were end-to-end aligned to the coding sequences (CDSs) of gene models using STAR 2.5.2b software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Dobin A, Davis C, Schlesinger F, Drenkow J, Zaleski C, Jha S, et al. STAR: ultrafast universal RNA-seq aligner. Bioinformatics. 2013; 29:15–21." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4855">62</a>] with default parameters. Reads that were mapped to multiple locations were excluded. The resulting mapped reads for each gene were normalized and patterns of gene expression between tissues were analyzed using DESeq2 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Love M, Huber W, Anders S. Moderated estimation of fold change and dispersion for RNA-seq data with DESeq2. Genome Biol. 2014;15:550." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4858">63</a>] and MCLUST version 3 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Fraley C, Raftery A. MCLUST version 3: an R package for normal mixture modeling and model-based clustering. Technical report no 504 Department of Statistics. Seattle: University of Washington; 2006." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4861">64</a>] that are included in the R/Bioconductor package. The data of three biological replicates were pooled and the average normalized read count values for genes were extracted and analyzed. Alternative splicing variants were analyzed using Cuffdiff2 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Trapnell C, Hendrickson D, Sauvageau M, Goff L, Rinn J, Pachter L. Differential analysis of gene regulation at transcript resolution with RNA-seq. Nat Biotechnol. 2013;31:46–53." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4864">65</a>] and spliceR [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Vitting-Seerup K, Porse B, Sandelin A, Waage J. spliceR: an R package for classification of alternative splicing and prediction of coding potential from RNA-seq data. BMC Bioinformatics. 2014;15:81." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4867">66</a>]. A genome-wide synteny comparison between Pyn and Pa, Pm, or Pp was performed based on an all-against-all BLASTP comparison (E value cutoff of 1E<sup>−10</sup>) and synteny regions were inferred using the MCScanX toolkit [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Wang Y, Tang H, DeBarry J, Tan X, Li J, Wang X, et al. MCScanX: a toolkit for detection and evolutionary analysis of gene synteny and collinearity. Nucleic Acids Res. 2012;40:e49." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4873">27</a>] with a match score of 50, match size of 5, and gap penalty of − 1. Orthologous gene families among the <i>Prunus</i> genomes were identified using OrthoMCL v2.0 software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="Fischer S, Brunk B, Chen F, Gao X, Harb O, Iodice JB, et al. Using OrthoMCL to assign proteins to OrthoMCL-DB groups or to cluster proteomes into new ortholog groups. Curr Protoc Bioinformatics. 2011;35:6.12.1–16.12.19." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4879">67</a>] with all-against-all BLASTP (E value cutoff of 1E<sup>−5</sup> and &gt; 50% match) searches. Gene family comparison between the <i>Prunus</i> genomes was performed using the PLAZA 3.0 Dicots database [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="Proost S, Van Bel M, Vaneechoutte D, Van de Peer Y, Inzé D, Mueller-Roeber B, et al. PLAZA 3.0: an access point for plant comparative genomics. Nucleic Acid Res. 2015;43:D974–81." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4888">68</a>]. Genome to genome synteny blocks of Pyn versus Pp, Pa, and Pm were plotted using an in-house perl script. For phylogenetic analysis of gene families, the amino acid sequences of orthologous genes were aligned using MUSCLE v3.8.31 software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="Edgar R. MUSCLE: multiple sequence alignment with high accuracy and high throughput. Nucleic Acids Res. 2004;32:1792–7." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4891">69</a>] with default parameters. Aligned sequences were trimmed at both ends using GBLOCKS 0.91b software to eliminate regions of poor alignment [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="Talavera G, Castresana J. Improvement of phylogenies after removing divergent and ambiguously aligned blocks from protein sequence alignments. Syst Biol. 2007;56:564–77." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4894">70</a>]. Conserved blocks of aligned sequences were concatenated into a single sequence and phylogenetic trees were constructed using the ML method in MEGA7 software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="Kumar S, Stecher G, Tamura K. MEGA7: molecular evolutionary genetics analysis version 7.0 for bigger datasets. Mol Biol Evol. 2016;33:1870–4." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4897">71</a>]. The stability of each tree node was tested by bootstrap analysis with 1000 replicates. Ks between homologous genes was determined using the PAML package [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 72" title="Yang Z. PAML 4: phylogenetic analysis by maximum likelihood. Mol Biol Evol. 2007;24:1586–91." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR72" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4900">72</a>].</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec17">Molecular dating</h3><p>To estimate the divergence time of the <i>Prunus</i> genomes, a total of 276 single copy orthologous genes, conserved in four <i>Prunus</i> species (Pyn, Pa, Pm, and Pp), two Rosaceae species (Mxd and Fv), and one outgroup Fabaceae species (Mt), were selected using reciprocal BLASTP with an E value cutoff of 1E<sup>−10</sup> and query coverage of 70%. For Bayesian evolutionary analysis, BEAST v1.7 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 73" title="Drummond A, Rambaut A. BEAST: Bayesian evolutionary analysis by sampling trees. BMC Evol Biol. 2007;7:214." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR73" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4920">73</a>] was used. Input files were generated by BEAUti interface with a GTR + I + G model and the combined dataset was applied for the BEAST analysis with a Yule speciation tree and an uncorrelated lognormal molecular clock model. We constrained the crown age of Rosaceae-Fabaceae with a uniform distribution from 100 to 107 Mya, following Moore et al. [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 74" title="Moore M, Soltis P, Bell C, Burleigh J, Soltis D. Phylogenetic analysis of 83 plastid genes resolves relationships among major clades of eudicot angiosperms and reveals multiple rapid radiations. Proc Natl Acad Sci U S A. 2010;107:4623–8." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4923">74</a>]. In addition, we applied two calibration points, following Chin et al. [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Chin S-W, Shaw J, Haberle R, Wen J, Potter D. Diversification of almonds, peaches, plums and cherries - molecular systematics and biogeographic history of Prunus (Rosaceae). Mol Phylogenet Evol. 2014;76:34–48." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4927">28</a>], each with a uniform distribution as follows: (1) the crown age of Rosaceae at 84.2–92.8 Mya; and (2) the crown age of <i>Prunus</i> at 51.6–65.2 Mya. Posterior distributions of parameters were approximated using two independent MCMC analyses of 20,000,000 generations with a 10% burn-in. The results were verified using Tracer v1.5 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="Tracer. &#xA;                    http://tree.bio.ed.ac.uk/software/tracer&#xA;                    &#xA;                  . Accessed 2 Apr 2018." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4933">75</a>] to ensure that plots from the two analyses converged on the same area and then combined. The samples from the posterior analysis were summarized on a maximum clade credibility tree, which had the maximum sum of posterior probabilities on its internal nodes using TreeAnnotator v1.5.4 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 73" title="Drummond A, Rambaut A. BEAST: Bayesian evolutionary analysis by sampling trees. BMC Evol Biol. 2007;7:214." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR73" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4936">73</a>] with the posterior probability limit set to 0.5. Means and 95% HPD of age estimates were obtained from the combined outputs using Tracer. The results were visualized using FigTree v1.4.2 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 76" title="FigTree. &#xA;                    http://tree.bio.ed.ac.uk/software/figtree&#xA;                    &#xA;                  . Accessed 2 Apr 2018." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR76" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4939">76</a>].</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec18">Resequencing, haplotype phasing, and variation analysis</h3><p>Five Pyn accessions from Jeju Island, Korea, four “Yoshino cherry” accessions (Pxy) from Tokyo, Japan, and Washington, DC, USA, and seven accessions of closely related species of Pyn, including Pjj, Pjq, Ppa, and Psa, were selected for resequencing analysis (Additional file <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#MOESM11">11</a>: Table S10). gDNA was extracted from the leaves of each accession as described above. Sequencing was performed by Illumina MiSeq, NextSeq or HiSeq (Illumina, San Diego, CA, USA) PE sequencing of libraries with 500-bp inserts according to the manufacturer’s protocol. At least 7.5× coverage of sequences was generated for each accession. All reads were preprocessed as mentioned above for quality. The genome size of each plant was calculated using the filtered reads as described above based on K-mer 17. For variome analysis, the filtered reads were aligned to the draft Pyn assembly using BWA-MEM 0.7.12 software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 77" title="Aligning sequence reads, clone sequences and assembly contigs with BWA-MEM. &#xA;                    https://arxiv.org/pdf/1303.3997v2.pdf&#xA;                    &#xA;                  . Accessed 24 Aug 2017." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR77" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4953">77</a>] with a parameter of M. Duplicate alignments were removed using the MarkDuplicates module in the Picard 2.2.4 package [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 78" title="Picard. &#xA;                    http://broadinstitute.github.io/picard&#xA;                    &#xA;                  . Accessed 24 Aug 2017." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR78" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4956">78</a>]. Realignment around short InDels and SNP genotyping were performed using RealignerTargetCreator, IndelRealigner, and HaplotypeCaller modules in GATK 3.7 software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 79" title="McKenna A, Hanna M, Banks E, Sivachenko A, Cibulskis K, Kernytsky A, et al. The genome analysis toolkit: a MapReduce framework for analyzing next-generation DNA sequencing data. Genome Res. 2010;20:1297–303." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR79" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4959">79</a>]. Annotation of SNPs and InDels was performed using SnpEff 4.3p software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 80" title="Cingolani P, Platts A, Wang L, Coon M, Nguyen T, Wang L, et al. A program for annotating and predicting the effects of single nucleotide polymorphisms, SnpEff: SNPs in the genome of Drosophila melanogaster strain w1118; iso-2; iso-3. Fly (Austin). 2012;6:80–92." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR80" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4962">80</a>]. For haplotype phasing of SNPs, SNP positions with a minimum depth of two reads were considered. BEDTools 2.25 software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 81" title="Quinlan A, Hall I. BEDTools: a flexible suite of utilities for comparing genomic features. Bioinformatics. 2010;26:841–2." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR81" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4966">81</a>] was used to compute the alignment coverage of maternal (Ppa) and paternal (Pjj) reads to the reference sequences. To determine the phased haplotype of SNPs and to impute missing genotype calls for the draft genome sequences, BEAGLE v4.0 software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 82" title="Browning S, Browning B. Rapid and accurate haplotype phasing and missing-data inference for whole-genome association studies by use of localized haplotype clustering. Am J Hum Genet. 2007;81:1084–97." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR82" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4969">82</a>] was used under default parameters. For further analysis of genic region, genes were phased into one of the parental types if a gene was aligned only by reads from one parent species or had at least twofold as many supports for SNPs by reads of one parental species. Otherwise, genes were defined as common type. MDS for two dimensions based on a pairwise distance matrix between two different genotypes was performed by PLINK software [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 83" title="Purcell S, Neale B, Todd-Brown K, Thomas L, Ferreira M, Bender D, et al. PLINK: a tool set for whole-genome association and population-based linkage analyses. Am J Hum Genet. 2007;81:559–75." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR83" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4972">83</a>] with the parameter of −genome, −cluster, −mds-plot 2. The MDS plots were drawn using R script. MEGA7 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="Kumar S, Stecher G, Tamura K. MEGA7: molecular evolutionary genetics analysis version 7.0 for bigger datasets. Mol Biol Evol. 2016;33:1870–4." href="/articles/10.1186/s13059-018-1497-y#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d65078e4975">71</a>] was used to draw an ML tree based on a pairwise distance matrix of SNPs, which was calculated by counting the total number of different alleles between genotypes.</p></div></div></section>

                      <i>Medicago truncatula</i>
                    </p>
                  </dd><dt class="c-abbreviation_list__term"><dfn>Mxd:</dfn></dt><dd class="c-abbreviation_list__description">
                    <p><i>Malus</i> х <i>domestica</i></p>
                  </dd><dt class="c-abbreviation_list__term"><dfn>Mya:</dfn></dt><dd class="c-abbreviation_list__description">
                    <p>Million years ago</p>
                  </dd><dt class="c-abbreviation_list__term"><dfn>NCBI:</dfn></dt><dd class="c-abbreviation_list__description">
                    <p>National Center for Biotechnology Information</p>
                  </dd><dt class="c-abbreviation_list__term"><dfn>NGS:</dfn></dt><dd class="c-abbreviation_list__description">
